  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4fbf8630-7e94-4be8-92d0-a4a8835b1499'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer7803135772089849138"><i>The Dragon Reborn</i>—the leader long prophesied who will save the world, but in the saving destroy it; the savior who will run mad and kill all those dearest to him—is on the run from his destiny.<br/><br/>Able to touch the One Power, but unable to control it, and with no one to teach him how—for no man has done it in three thousand years—Rand al'Thor knows only that he must face the D</span>
  <span id="freeText7803135772089849138" style="display:none"><i>The Dragon Reborn</i>—the leader long prophesied who will save the world, but in the saving destroy it; the savior who will run mad and kill all those dearest to him—is on the run from his destiny.<br /><br />Able to touch the One Power, but unable to control it, and with no one to teach him how—for no man has done it in three thousand years—Rand al'Thor knows only that he must face the Dark One. But how?<br /><br />Winter has stopped the war—almost—yet men are dying, calling out for the Dragon. But where is he?<br /><br />Perrin Aybara is in pursuit with Moiraine Sedai, her Warder Lan, and Loial the Ogier. Bedeviled by dreams, Perrin is grappling with another deadly problem—how is he to escape the loss of his own humanity?<br /><br />Egwene, Elayne and Nynaeve are approaching Tar Valon, where Mat will be healed—if he lives until they arrive. But who will tell the Amyrlin their news—that the Black Ajah, long thought only a hideous rumor, is all too real? They cannot know that in Tar Valon far worse awaits...<br /><br />Ahead, for all of them, in the Heart of the Stone, lies the next great test of the Dragon reborn....<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7803135772089849138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/83875380-sky">Sky</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I don't think the vocabulary is particularly complex. The book contains a lot of very detailed descriptions of people and environments, but I think th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I don't think the vocabulary is particularly complex. The book contains a lot of very detailed descriptions of people and environments, but I think the language is generally easy to understand. On a sentence level, the structure is mostly straightforward. However, the author is very verbose. The language may be simple, but there is a lot of it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2361866479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2361866479" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2361866479?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8153990-the-dragon-reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2361866479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15154106749482958150"><b>3.5/5 stars<br/><br/>Not much actually happened in <i>The Dragon Reborn</i> but it was more engaging than the previous two books.</b><br/><br/><i>The Dragon Reborn</i> is the third book in <i>The Wheel of Time</i> by Robert Jordan. The title of this novel may be <i>The Dragon Reborn</i>, this title implies that Rand will take the central role again, but the main characters of this book were actually Mat, Perrin, and Egwene. If I’m not mistaken, Rand has only like three or four small POV chapters. This doesn’t mean that Rand wasn’t important to th</span>
  <span id="freeText15154106749482958150" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5 stars<br><br>Not much actually happened in <i>The Dragon Reborn</i> but it was more engaging than the previous two books.</b><br><br><i>The Dragon Reborn</i> is the third book in <i>The Wheel of Time</i> by Robert Jordan. The title of this novel may be <i>The Dragon Reborn</i>, this title implies that Rand will take the central role again, but the main characters of this book were actually Mat, Perrin, and Egwene. If I’m not mistaken, Rand has only like three or four small POV chapters. This doesn’t mean that Rand wasn’t important to the main story, the storyline still heavily revolved around him.<br><br><b>Picture: <i>The Dragon Reborn</i> by Francesca Resta</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1556879245i/27449171._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now that I’m three books into the series, let me just say that Jordan is terribly slow in progressing his main story, and the early books are supposedly some of Jordan’s finest works in the series; I haven’t reached the infamous dreadful book 7-10. If you cut/condensed the traveling sections of the first three books, what you have is pretty much one book with no pacing issue; Jordan is that inefficient and repetitive. That being said, <i>The Dragon Reborn</i> was, somehow, the most engaging book so far. Sure there was still repetition and same plot structure usage—started strong for the first 20%, travel for 50-60%, then closing with incredible final section—but I didn’t find myself struggling through the middle section as much as I did for the first two books. <br><br>I feel like Jordan has improved a lot in characterizations; I found Mat, Perrin, and Egwene to be more sympathetic than before now. Focusing the POV chapters to these three ended up being a great decision; it brings a lot of benefits rather than disadvantages. First of all, we get to read these important characters being developed further. We also get to see their thoughts towards Rand, other characters, and the state of the world/predicament they’re in. Finally, Rand was still thickheaded here and I don’t think I can withstand reading him being stubborn about accepting his destiny for another 700 pages for the third time in a row. I get it, he has valid reasons for being stubborn and reluctant, and I do understand why he acted that way. However, just because I understand his reasons doesn’t mean that I would enjoy reading literally thousands of pages of him being angry and stubborn about something which he always ended up doing anyway.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Should and would build no bridges.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>This was the first time where I started to realize just how insane Nynaeve’s braid tugging syndrome was. Insane, I mean it, insane and ridiculous. Not only she’s one of the most annoying female characters I’ve ever encountered (and there are still 10 books left for her to get worse), her existence relies dangerously on her tugging braid. I can’t seem to understand why Jordan need to emphasize her braid tugging that much, it was pointless and annoying; I think she’ll literally die if she doesn’t tug her braid. No one in the world tugs their braid that fiercely and that much. NO ONE.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“She jerked her braid so hard it hurt.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>*standing applause*<br><br>As much as I enjoyed reading this installment, I seriously feel like not a lot of important things have happened; the entirety of the three books so far could’ve been easily condensed into one book without losing matters of importance. I’m giving the same 3.5 stars rating just like I did for the first two books. In my opinion, that’s not a good enough measurement for a series as massive as this. Why am I continuing? I loved Sanderson’s adult fantasy works that much that I’m willing to push myself—or at least still attempt—to finish this series just to read Sanderson’s involvement in it. Although I sounded negative and critical in this review, let me clarify that it wasn’t because it’s a bad book, <i>The Dragon Reborn</i> was the least boring installment so far. I just feel disappointed that a lot of the superb parts of the series so far were constantly diminished unnecessarily due to pacing issue and repetitiveness. I’ve heard a lot of amazing things about the next book of the series, <i>The Shadow Rising</i>, here’s hoping that it will finally break or at least reached my 4 stars rating barrier. <br><br><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780765334350/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br><br><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/05/03/the-dragon-reborn-the-wheel-of-time-3/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15154106749482958150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1497881147" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1497881147" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1497881147?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780356503844" href="/book/show/22369403-the-dragon-reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1497881147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18179994356403881924">This was a hugely important book for me. This is a fourteen book series, and after the last book I was practically ready to stop reading it. I had to have a six month reading break because I was that frustrated with it. I thought that Rand was characterised horrendously, and I felt that he regressed to an early state. All in all, Robert Jordan had gone backward in his character development of his hero. So, this book had to win me over to keep me reading.<br/><br/>And it did. It so bloody-well did. My fait</span>
  <span id="freeText18179994356403881924" style="display:none">This was a hugely important book for me. This is a fourteen book series, and after the last book I was practically ready to stop reading it. I had to have a six month reading break because I was that frustrated with it. I thought that Rand was characterised horrendously, and I felt that he regressed to an early state. All in all, Robert Jordan had gone backward in his character development of his hero. So, this book had to win me over to keep me reading.<br><br>And it did. It so bloody-well did. My faith in the author has been completely restored. (Yay!) Rand is still the same heroic coward, but this time his actions actually corresponded with the events. When he ran, he had reason to do so. He also had very few point of view chapters. He is still the centre of the story, but its telling is given over to much more interesting characters like Mat, Nynaeve and my personal favourite Perrin. So, let’s starts with the best character. <br><br><b> He has the heart of a wolf </b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453038864i/17775196._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The book opens with Perrin. It’s still very early days, but he is one of the only characters I actually have sympathy for. His confidence has developed even further. When he taps the ancient magic that allows him to communicate with wolves, they run to his aid and welcome him as leader of their pack. This is a worthy boon for the young warrior, but it doesn’t come without its problems. The ability alters his mind; it makes him feral as the wolfish thoughts dominate his human senses. He knows the danger of the ability; thus, he suppresses it and controls it. I find his part of the story completely fascinating because he boarders on edges of remaining noble and good or loosing himself to animalistic savagery. <br><br><i>Moraine was silent for a time, warming her hands. Finally she spoke whilst staring into the flames. ‘The Creator is good, Perrin. The Farther of Lies is evil. The Pattern of Age, the Age Lace itself, is neither. The pattern is what is. The Wheel of Time weaves all lives into the Pattern, all actions. A Pattern that is all one colour is no pattern. For the Pattern of an age, good and ill are the warp and the woof.’</i><br><br>Moreover, in this bleak and dark world that Jordan has created, Perrin is one of the few with a pure heart, which makes his inner darkness even more complex. Like Rand and Mat, he wants to hang up his weapons and go home; he wants to forget about the long and hard task the wheel has set for him, but he knows what he must do. He knows that he cannot run; he knows that he cannot escape fate. So, he grits his teeth and gets on with his duty. After all, he will have an important part to play in defeating the darkness. He is too honourable to shirk from what he must perform. I can see him eventually becoming the rock that holds the trio together. He is a well-rounded character that is reliable and strong. I just know that he will have the courage to insure that his friends succeed, even if he has to drag them to their destiny. <br><br><b> Finally, some decent female characters. </b><br><br>Admittedly, for the first time in this series, I actually enjoyed the female side of the story. Previously, it seemed like Jordan could only write females in one way; they were all confrontational, moody, hot headed, physically attractive and at times even quite spiteful. It was beginning to get a little bit ridiculous; it was like he somehow naively perceived that all women have this same archetypal personality. This was regardless of their social standing or life experience. All the female characters were basically the same misogynistic reused stereotype. Thankfully, and at long last, Jordan’s women are actually developing their own sense of individualism. It took him long enough to get there, now they're finally out of the tower. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453039131i/17775235._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, anyway, the girls are coming into there own. Nynaeve has had heaps of character development. She’s learning to wield her magic to deadly affect, but she still hasn’t quite figured how to activate it properly. She can only use it when in a state of pure agitation and anger. It responds to rage and rage only. When it is eventually unleashed it is powerful to behold, but not controlled. She’s a strong character, and a very strong woman. She’s quickly become the leader of the naïve Egwene and the inexperienced Elayne. She has the experience, and the wisdom (see what I did there?) to lead them in their hunt for the twisted Black Ajah. It was great to see these characters have their own fully developed side story that eventually linked back to the main plot. And the same is true for the cunning Mat. <br><br><b> Every perfect fantasy story needs it rouge </b> <br><br>Mat has also come along way. He’s recovered from his illness, though there is still some degree of taint in his heart. He has memories that are not his own. It will be interesting to see how this develops in later books, as the true origin of his luck will hopefully be revealed. The two are clearly connected and intertwined. He is a strong character, one who is developing faster than he can handle. He’s already killed countless men, which is something he would never have thought himself capable. He has the danger of becoming numb to it as many fall to his agile wielding of his quarter staff. <br><br>This was a really good book, and I’m so glad. I’m actually looking forward to reading the next one. The side characters really make this series worthwhile. If you ignore Rand, like I‘m trying to do, you will see how complex and versatile these other characters are. Their stories are much more interesting on every level. The world is also rich in opposing culture and beliefs. I like the way the “forces of good” are divided and mistrusting of each other. The Children of the Light are potentially morally right, but they are misguided and confused as to what is actually evil. Their ethos is right, though they just execute it in a roundabout way. It will be interesting to see if they become pawns of the dark one or see the error of their ways. I love these conflicting ideas. <br><br>So, for me, this series remains in the realms of perfect fantasy. At least, at the moment. Hopefully, it will remain good to its end. <br><br><u>The Wheel of time: </u><br> 1. Eye of the World- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1002483199?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">An unoriginal five stars</a><br>2. The Great Hunt- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1360033546" rel="nofollow noopener"> A reluctant three stars</a><br>3. The Dragon Reborn- <b>A well-developed 4 stars.</b> <br>4. The Shadow Rising- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1982182213?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">A strong four stars</a><br>5. The Fires of Heaven- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2391618242?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A slow two stars</a><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1436177441p8/1205774.jpg" width="400" height="216" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>
  <b>“Kill a man who needs killing, and sometimes others pay for it. The question is, was it worth doing it anyway? There's always a balance, you know. Good and evil. Light and Shadow. We would not be human if there wasn't a balance.” </b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18179994356403881924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText9805925973101837296" style="display:none">DNF @ 30%<br /><br />Dear Wheel of time I am breaking up with you.<br /><br />This wasn't easy decision as I don't like to leave things unfinished.My friends keep on telling me how great you are and that I should give you another chance but I think that this relationship has already taken too much of my time and I just can't look past your snail pace and many obnoxious characters.We definitively had our good moments but every time we are together I keep thinking about other series and keep glancing on other books on my shelf and that is not how relationship between reader and book should be.Call me old fashioned but I believe book should hold the reader tight and make him forget about other books until the last page is done.<br /><br />I am sure you will find devoted reader who will adore you and maybe our paths well cross again and we continue from where we left but I just can't see it happening anytime soon.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13374110748613696241"><b>3/7/16:</b> WoT #3 buddy (re)read in <b>

LOVE it. <br/><br/><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/04/review-the-dragon-reborn-by-robert-jordan.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>NOTICE:</b> this reread is in preparation for finally biting the bullet and reading book 14. That means I HAVE NOT read book 14 yet. Please be mindful of this in the comments, both for me and for others who may or may not have progressed past this point in the series.   <span id="freeText13374110748613696241" style="display:none"><b>3/7/16:</b> WoT #3 buddy (re)read in <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">BB&amp;B</a>
</b>! I'm thinking I might read it again just b/c. LOVE it. <br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/04/review-the-dragon-reborn-by-robert-jordan.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>NOTICE:</b> this reread is in preparation for finally biting the bullet and reading book 14. That means I HAVE NOT read book 14 yet. Please be mindful of this in the comments, both for me and for others who may or may not have progressed past this point in the series. Thank you.<br><br><i>The Dragon Reborn</i> is where things <i>really</i> start getting good. <br><br>PLEASE NOTE that I am speaking strictly from the REREAD perspective. If you have never read the series before, the first two books are spectacular. Spectacular x5, even. It's only knowing what's coming and being impatient to get to the <i>even better</i> parts that makes books 1 and 2 merely enjoyable when compared to the depth of imagination and interconnectedness as the series progresses.<br><br>BUT. All of that epicness must have a solid foundation on which to build.<br><br>And book #3 is still very much a part of that early foundation-laying process. <br><br>However, TWO very important things happen in this installment (and those two things make all the difference):<br><br>1. Mat is healed from the taint of the Shadar Logoth dagger.<br>2. Perrin meets Faile.<br><br>I don't know if prior-to-book 3-Mat was part of Jordan's character growth process, or if he just got bored with the character--I certainly found the early version to be tiresome--but when Mat wakes from being Healed in Tar Valon, he's almost a completely different person. <br><br>Oh, he's still a rascal, but no longer a rascal of the juvenile variety. Instead, he becomes that kind of clever, scalawag, rogue-type character, who has always been one of my personal favorites. <br><br>In another life (HA!), he would have made an <i>excellent</i> pirate.<br><br>It's the difference between telling a couple of younger boys a story about ghost hounds, then covering a few dogs in flour and loosing them on the village green, and betting Galad and Gawyn that he can beat them, his quarterstaff against their two swords, both b/c he needs the money to finance his escape, and also b/c "it would be fun."<br><br>Then there's Faile. <br><br>A lot of WoT fans aren't particularly fond of Faile, and maybe I'll change my mind after rereading some of the later installments . . . but I doubt it.<br><br>I just like her.<br><br>Firstly, she's Saldaean, which is my second favorite people group (after the Aiel). <br><br>Almost all of the drama in her relationship with Perrin can be attributed to her nationality, and where others are simply exhausted by her and her antics, I chalk it up to cultural differences. &lt;------legit cause for misunderstandings.<br><br>And when she's not behaving in what a non-Saldaean would consider a ridiculous manner, her interactions with Perrin are positively delightful; I am full of delight.<br><br>Her appearance is also the first concrete manifestation (with long-term consequences) of one of Min's Viewings. <br><br>So yeah, those two things are where I turn the corner and stop fighting the urge to skim things I've read <i>numerous</i> times before.<br><br>This book is also where the Forsaken start to become real characters instead of flat boogiemen-type shapes. <br><br>In <i>The Eye of the World</i>, we learned nothing beyond the fact that some of them were no longer imprisoned, and that there were two fewer of them in world. In <i>The Great Hunt</i>, the information was limited to Lanfear. But in <i>The Dragon Reborn</i>, we not only learn more about Lanfear, we also meet at least three others, <i>and</i> some of the mystery surrounding "Ba’alzamon" is . . . not <i>revealed</i>, per se, but I definitely felt I understood what the situation was by the time I finished the book. <br><br>And anytime we learn anything about the Age of Legends (whence the Forsaken came), I am a happy camper.<br><br>Basically, I loved it. <br><br>PS: is it just me, or does Cover Dude bear a remarkable resemblance to Prince Harry?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/705725321" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eye of the World (Wheel of Time, #1) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373567" rel="nofollow noopener">The Great Hunt (Wheel of Time, #2) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373656" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow Rising (Wheel of Time, #4) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373676" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fires of Heaven (Wheel of Time, #5) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373711" rel="nofollow noopener">Lord of Chaos (Wheel of Time, #6) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373844" rel="nofollow noopener">A Crown of Swords (Wheel of Time, #7) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373921" rel="nofollow noopener">The Path of Daggers (Wheel of Time, #8) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404373936" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter's Heart (Wheel of Time, #9) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404374050" rel="nofollow noopener">Crossroads of Twilight (Wheel of Time, #10) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404374100" rel="nofollow noopener">New Spring (Wheel of Time, #0) by Robert Jordan</a>
</b><br><br><b>Highlights:</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1. Mat HEALED!! WOOT!<br><br>2. Egwene's Accepted Test.<br><br>3. Mat with a quarterstaff vs. Galad and Gawyn with swords. Like . . . a day after he'd been Healed. EPIC. One of my favorite scenes from the whole series.<br><br>4. FAILE.<br><br>5. Mat rescuing Nynaeve, Egwene, and Elayne.<br><br>6. <i>He raised <b>Callandor</b> above his head. Silver lightning crackled from the blade, jagged streaks arching toward the great dome above. “Stop!” he shouted. The fighting ceased; men stared at him in wonder, over black veils, from beneath the rims of round helmets. “I am Rand al’Thor!” he called, so his voice rang through the chamber. “I am the Dragon Reborn!” <b>Callandor</b> shone in his grasp. <br>One by one, veiled men and helmeted, they knelt to him, crying, “The Dragon is Reborn! The Dragon is Reborn!”</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Forsaken:</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1. <i>He hated Illian. “One day we’ll loot Illian bare, tear down every town and village, and sow their filthy ground with salt.” Mallia’s beard almost bristled with outrage at how filthy the Illian land was. “Even their olives are putrid! One day we’ll carry every last Illianer pig off in chains! That is what the <b>High Lord Samon</b> says.”</i><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Be'lal. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>2. <i>Before he could find words, the door crashed back against the wall, and Moiraine stood in the doorway, her face as pale and grim as death. “<b>Your wolf dreams tell as truly as a Dreamer’s, Perrin</b>. The Forsaken <b>are</b> loose, and one of them rules in Illian.” <br>Perrin climbed off the bed and started dressing, not caring whether Zarine was watching or not. He knew what he intended to do, but he asked Moiraine anyway. “Do we leave?” <br>“Unless you want to make closer acquaintance with <b>Sammael</b>,” she said dryly.</i><br><br>3. <i>“Be silent, boy,” the dark man in the gold-encrusted coat said calmly. He was a handsome man, almost as good-looking as Galad and nearly as youthful-seeming, despite the white streaking his temples, but built on a bigger scale, with more than Rand’s height and very nearly Perrin’s shoulders. “We will hear what you have to say in a moment.” He reached over Morgase’s shoulder and plucked the letter out of her hand. Her glare turned on him—Mat could see her temper heating—but the dark man laid a strong hand on her shoulder, never taking his eyes off what he was reading, and Morgase’s anger melted. “It seems she has left the Tower again,” he said. “On the service of the Amyrlin Seat. The woman oversteps herself again, Morgase.” <br>Mat had no trouble holding his tongue. <b>Luck</b>. It was stuck to the roof of his mouth. <b>Sometimes I don’t know if it’s good or bad</b>. The dark man was the owner of the deep voice, the “Great Master” who wanted Elayne’s head. <b>She called him Gaebril. Her advisor wants to murder Elayne? Light</b>! And Morgase was staring up at him like an adoring dog with her master’s hand on her shoulder.</i><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rahvin. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>4. <i>“One of the Forsaken is in Tear. The High Lord Samon is <b>Be’lal</b>.”</i><br><br>5. <i>“I will not be undone!” Ba’alzamon cried. His mouth was fire; his shriek echoed among the columns. “I cannot be defeated! Aid me!” Some of the darkness shrouding him drifted into his hands, formed into a ball so black it seemed to soak up even the light of <b>Callandor</b>. Sudden triumph blazed in the flames of his eyes. <br>“You are destroyed!” Rand shouted. <b>Callandor</b> spun in his hands. Its light roiled the darkness, severed the steel-black lines around Ba’alzamon, and Ba’alzamon convulsed. As if there were two of him he seemed to dwindle and grow larger at the same time. “You are undone!” Rand plunged the shining blade into Ba’alzamon’s chest. <br>Ba’alzamon screamed, and the fires of his face flared wildly. “Fool!” he howled. “The Great Lord of the Dark can never be defeated!” <br>Rand pulled <b>Callandor</b>’s blade free as Ba’alzamon’s body sagged and began to fall, the shadow around him vanishing. <br>And suddenly Rand was in another Heart of the Stone, surrounded by columns still whole, and fighting men screaming and dying, veiled men and men in breastplates and helmets. Moiraine still lay crumpled at the base of a redstone column. And at Rand’s feet lay the body of a man, sprawled on its back with a hole burned through the chest. He might have been a handsome man in his middle years, except that where his eyes and mouth should have been were only pits from which rose tendrils of black smoke. </i><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ba’alzamon = Ishamael. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Foresight:</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1. <i><b>Only a dream</b>, he thought, shivering from the cold, and with that everything shifted. <br>He stared into the mirror, a part of him not comprehending what he saw, another part accepting. <b>A gilded helmet, worked like a lion’s head, sat on his head as if it belonged there. Gold leaf covered his ornately hammered breastplate, and gold-work embellished the plate and mail on his arms and legs</b>. Only the axe at his side was plain. A voice—his own—whispered in his mind that he would take it over any other weapon, had carried it a thousand times, in a hundred battles. <b>No</b>! He wanted to take it off, throw it away. <b>I can’t</b>!</i><br><br>2. <i>“An Aielman in a cage,” she said promptly. “A Tuatha’an with a sword. A falcon and a hawk, perching on your shoulders. Both female, I think. And all the rest, of course. What is always there. Darkness swirling ’round you, and—”</i><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1. Gaul<br>2. Aram<br>3.a. Faile<br>3.b. Berelain  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>3. <i>" ‘Heart of the Dark. Ba’alzamon. Name hidden within name shrouded by name. Secret buried within secret cloaked by secret. Betrayer of Hope. Ishamael betrays all hope. Truth burns and sears. Hope fails before truth. A lie is our shield. Who can stand against the Heart of the Dark? Who can face the Betrayer of Hope? Soul of shadow, Soul of the Shadow, he is—’ ”</i><br><br>4. <i>“Tell me why,” she demanded. “Why would you ask me to—to murder you? I will Heal you, I will do anything to get you out of there, but I cannot kill you. Why?” <br>“<b>They can turn me, Egwene</b>.” His breathing was so tortured, she wished she could weep. “<b>If they take me—the Myrddraal—the Dreadlords—they can turn me to the Shadow</b>. If madness has me, I cannot fight them. I won’t know what they are doing till it is too late. If there is even a spark of life left when they find me, they can still do it. Please, Egwene. For the love of the Light. Kill me.”<br><br>Sheriam sighed, glanced at the other Aes Sedai again, then dropped her voice to a whisper and spoke swiftly. “This is something known only to a few, child, even in the Tower. You should not learn it now, if ever, but I will tell you. <b>There is—a weakness in being able to channel. That we learn to open ourselves to the True Source means that we can be—opened to other things</b>.” Egwene shuddered. “Calm yourself, child. It is not so easily done. It is a thing not done, so far as I know—Light send it has not been done!—since the Trolloc Wars. <b>It took thirteen Dreadlords—Darkfriends who could channel—weaving the flows through thirteen Myrddraal</b>. You see? Not easily done."</i><br><br>5. <i>"<b>Where are you from, lad?” <br>“Manetheren</b>.” Mat froze when he heard the name come out of his mouth. “I mean, I’m from the Two Rivers. I have heard too many old stories.”</i><br><br>6. <i>There had been a dream of Rand, reaching for a sword that seemed to be made of crystal, never seeing the fine net dropping over him. And one of him kneeling in a chamber where a parched wind blew dust across the floor, and creatures like the one on the Dragon banner, but much smaller, floated on that wind, and settled into his skin. There had been a dream of him walking down into a great hole in a black mountain, a hole filled with a reddish glare as from vast fires below, and even a dream of him confronting Seanchan.<br><br>Perrin with a falcon on his shoulder, and Perrin with a hawk. Only the hawk held a leash in her talons—Egwene was somehow convinced both hawk and falcon were female—and the hawk was trying to fasten it around Perrin’s neck.<br><br>And that dream of Perrin—with a beard!—leading a huge pack of wolves that stretched as far as the eye could see.<br><br>Mat, placing his own left eye on a balance scale. Mat, hanging by his neck from a tree limb.</i><br><br>7. <i>“<b>Farmboy! Perhaps I will call myself Faile. My father used to call me that, when I was little. It means ‘falcon</b>.’ ” <br>He stiffened and almost missed the first step of the ladder. <b>Coincidence</b>. He made himself go down without looking back toward her. <b>It has to be</b>.</i><br><br>8. <i>There had been dreams of Mat, too. Of Mat with dice spinning ’round him—she felt she knew where that one came from—of Mat being followed by a man who was not there—she still did not understand that; there was a man following, or maybe more than one, but in some way there was no one there—of Mat riding desperately toward something unseen in the distance that he had to reach, and Mat with a woman who seemed to be tossing fireworks about. An Illuminator, she assumed, but that made no more sense than anything else.</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Insight:</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1. <i>A dozen small things besides, some perhaps only baseless rumors, but taken together with the rest . . . Sightings of Aiel reported as far west as Murandy, and Kandor. Only two or three in one place, but one or a thousand, Aiel had come out of the Waste just once in all the years since the Breaking. Only in the Aiel War had they ever left that desolate wilderness.<br><br>The Atha’an Miere, the Sea Folk, were said to be ignoring trade to seek signs and portents—of what, exactly, they did not say—sailing with ships half full or even empty.<br><br>Illian had called the Great Hunt of the Horn for the first time in almost four hundred years, had sent out the Hunters to seek the fabled Horn of Valere, which prophecy said would summon dead heroes from the grave to fight in Tarmon Gai’don, the Last Battle against the Shadow.<br><br>Rumor said the Ogier, always so reclusive that most common people thought them only legend, had called meetings between their far-flung <b>stedding</b>.</i><br><br>2. <i>“Browns seek knowledge, Blues meddle in causes, and Whites consider the questions of truth with implacable logic. We all do some of it all, of course. But to be a Green means to stand ready.” A note of pride entered Alanna’s voice. “In the Trolloc Wars, we were often called the Battle Ajah. All Aes Sedai helped where and when they could, but the Green Ajah alone was always with the armies, in almost every battle. We were the counter to the Dreadlords. The Battle Ajah. And now we stand ready, for the Trollocs to come south again, for Tarmon Gai’don, the Last Battle. We will be there. That is what it means to be a Green.”</i><br><br>3. <i>If dogs had been able to make footprints on stone, he would have said it was the print of a large hound. There were no hound’s footprints in any of the bare ground he could see, where softer dirt on the verge might take one, and no smell of any dog’s trail. Just a faint trace in the air of something burned, almost the sulphurous smell left by setting off fireworks.</i><br><br>4. <i>“Every queen of Manetheren was an Aes Sedai, and the king the Warder bound to her."</i><br><br>5. <i>Elayne nodded. “I think so. I do not know much of the Prophecies of the Dragon, but I have heard a few lines. One I remember is, ‘On the slopes of Dragonmount shall he be born, born of a maiden wedded to no man.’ Egwene, <b>Rand does look like an Aiel. Well, he looks like the pictures I have seen of Tigraine, too</b>, but she vanished before he was born, and I hardly think she could have been his mother anyway. I think Rand’s mother was a Maiden of the Spear.”</i><br><br>6. <i>Rhuarc cleared his throat. “When a man wishes to become a clan chief, he must go to Rhuidean, in the lands of the Jenn Aiel, the clan that is not.” He spoke slowly and frowned often at the red-fringed silk carpet under his soft boots, a man trying to explain what he did not want to explain at all. “Women who wish to become Wise Ones also make this journey, but their marking, if they are marked, is kept secret among themselves. The men who are chosen at Rhuidean, those who survive, return marked on the left arm. So.” <br>He pushed back the sleeves of his coat and shirt together to reveal his left forearm, the skin much paler than that of his hands and face. Etched into the skin as if part of it, wrapped twice around, marched the same gold-and-scarlet form as rippled on the banner above the Stone. <br>The Aiel let his sleeve fall with a sigh. “It is a name not spoken except among the clan chiefs and the Wise Ones. We are . . .” He cleared his throat again, unable to say it here. <br>“<b>The Aiel are the People of the Dragon</b>.”</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Musings:</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1. <i>Niall nodded grimly. There had been no male Aes Sedai since the Breaking of the World, but the women who still claimed that title were bad enough. They prated of their Three Oaths: to speak no word that was not true, to make no weapon for one man to kill another, to use the One Power as a weapon only against Darkfriends or Shadowspawn. But now they had showed those oaths for the lies they were. He had always known no one could want the power they wielded except to challenge the Creator, and that meant to serve the Dark One.</i><br><br>Whitecloaks are so freaking obnoxious. What do you mean, "no one could want the power they wielded"? It's not like they HAVE A CHOICE. *grumbles* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8153990-the-dragon-reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=2018">2018</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2423569879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5395406185644717924">While this book is titled Dragon Reborn, it definitely is not about Rand al’Thor as the title suggests. This book paves way for Mat, Perrin, and Egwene to shine. <br/><br/>Mat, Perrin, Rand, and Egwene all got their separate story arcs here as they all went their different ways in the start of the book. Rand appeared only in 2-3 chapters. So when Rand went in to Tear to take Callandor and put the rumours down for once and all; it was Mat, Perrin and the girl gang (Egwene, Nynaeve, Elyane) who took the cen</span>
  <span id="freeText5395406185644717924" style="display:none">While this book is titled Dragon Reborn, it definitely is not about Rand al’Thor as the title suggests. This book paves way for Mat, Perrin, and Egwene to shine. <br /><br />Mat, Perrin, Rand, and Egwene all got their separate story arcs here as they all went their different ways in the start of the book. Rand appeared only in 2-3 chapters. So when Rand went in to Tear to take Callandor and put the rumours down for once and all; it was Mat, Perrin and the girl gang (Egwene, Nynaeve, Elyane) who took the center stage here. <br /><br />While the girls were good, it was Perrin and Mat who won my heart in this book. Both guys finally came out of Rand’s shadow and surprised me. Perrin already holds a special place because of what he can do (and let’s not forget wolves) but Mat was the surprise package. I hated Mat from Book 1, so I am shocked how much I liked him here. He is witty, trouble-magnet, not so brave (he try his best to escape evil/difficult situations) but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ when he went into the tower to save the girls <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I turned into a fan.<br /><br />the book dragged in few chapters but Jordan surely knows how to write an amazing climax and all the different story lines and different prophecies converge beautifully in the end. <br /><br />All in all another great book in the long series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5395406185644717924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText16598971232678334348" style="display:none"><b>*** 5 *** </b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Til shade is gone,<br />til water is gone<br />Into the shadow with teeth bared<br />Screaming defiance with the last breath<br />To spit in Sightblinder’s eye on the Last Day.”<br />― Robert Jordan, The Dragon Reborn..."</i>

Writing a review, the way I fan-girl over this series, is absolutely worthless. I have no objectivity left and honestly, attempting to describe this intricate and complex plot seems to me an insurmountable task. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Heart of the Dark. Ba’alzamon. Name hidden within name shrouded by name. Secret buried within secret cloaked by secret. Betrayer of Hope. Ishamael betrays all hope. Truth burns and sears. Hope fails before truth. A lie is our shield. Who can stand against the Heart of the Dark? Who can face the Betrayer of Hope? Soul of shadow, Soul of the Shadow, he is—”<br />― Robert Jordan, The Dragon Reborn..."</i>
</b><br /><br />If you are even slightly interested in the genre of Classic Fantasy, or High Quest Fantasy, and I would say the restrictions of those labels are far outreached in this series, this should be a MUST READ!!! It starts slow, but instead of boring, it is entrancing with the masterful world building which unfolds natural in front of us... And the characters are so animated and real, that when away from the books, you actually miss them... Epic and entertaining. Read it!!!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Just because fate has chosen something for you instead of you choosing it for yourself doesn’t mean it has to be bad. <div id="review_2209827348" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2209827348" />
    <a title="Nimrod Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5175502-nimrod-daniel"><img alt="Nimrod Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344358412p2/5175502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2209827348?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nimrod Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nimrod Daniel" href="/user/show/5175502-nimrod-daniel">Nimrod Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8153990-the-dragon-reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5175502-nimrod-daniel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2209827348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6345191058871333629">A very compelling continuation of The Wheel of Time series, but not amazing as The Great hunt.<br/><br/>There’s a very interesting decision by Jordan to push Rand to the background so Mat and Perrin would shine in his absence and it worked very well. In The Great Hunt I felt like Perrin barely had a focus on him in comparison to The Eye of The World, and so as for Mat. Mat had even less focus than Perrin in the first 2 books, and both of them felt like nice additions to the cast but no more than that. In </span>
  <span id="freeText6345191058871333629" style="display:none">A very compelling continuation of The Wheel of Time series, but not amazing as The Great hunt.<br /><br />There’s a very interesting decision by Jordan to push Rand to the background so Mat and Perrin would shine in his absence and it worked very well. In The Great Hunt I felt like Perrin barely had a focus on him in comparison to The Eye of The World, and so as for Mat. Mat had even less focus than Perrin in the first 2 books, and both of them felt like nice additions to the cast but no more than that. In The Dragon Reborn it’s exactly the opposite, as they have quite a lot of POV chapters where they could grow into interesting characters, and their overall importance begins to emerge.<br />As for the rest of the characters – there’s still focus on Nynaeve and Egwene, both are really great characters., and probably my favorites. Elayne becomes a very important part of this trio, and the three of them keep growing and developing as characters. Moiraine and Lan were mostly in the background in book 2 but we see much more of them here, which is great.<br /><br />To that, pour some schemes by The Black Aja, The Forsaken are keep steering things in the world, and Ba’alzamon continues with his plans. Oh, and some ancient relics:)<br /><br />What I really liked in this book is the development of the world-building, as we find out more about the World of Dreams and Jordan even dabbled with parallel worlds ideas. That add a lot of possibilities for the series to go in interesting directions. As the series progresses it is evident that The Wheel of Time isn’t a formulaic generic fantasy, which is great, especially when considering when WoT was written. <br /><br />All in all, it’s a very good installment in the Wheel of Time series, with very good character development, fascinating world-building and pretty good plot(but not as good as in book 2).<br /><br />4.25/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="6345191058871333629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_793271566" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271566" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/793271566?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780812513714" href="/book/show/359820.The_Dragon_Reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=wheel-of-time">wheel-of-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793271566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11338417041515907225"><i>"The alarm gongs sent echoes crashing through the Stone, but Rand paid no more attention to them than he had to the roar that had come before, like muffled thunder from somewhere below. His side ached, the old wound burned, strained almost to tearing by the climb up the side of the fortress. He gave the pain no heed, either. A crooked smile was fixed on his face, a smile of anticipation and dread he could not have wiped away if he had wanted to. It was close now. What he had dreamed of. Callando</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11338417041515907225" style="display:none"><i>"The alarm gongs sent echoes crashing through the Stone, but Rand paid no more attention to them than he had to the roar that had come before, like muffled thunder from somewhere below. His side ached, the old wound burned, strained almost to tearing by the climb up the side of the fortress. He gave the pain no heed, either. A crooked smile was fixed on his face, a smile of anticipation and dread he could not have wiped away if he had wanted to. It was close now. What he had dreamed of. Callandor."</i><br /><br />Rand al'Thor has finally, and very reluctantly, embraced his destiny as the Dragon Reborn after the events at Almoth Plain. But his face is known throughout the nations now, and he is hunted relentlessly by the numerous followers of the Shadow. Thus begins a new journey, and at its end lies the Stone of Tear, the impregnable fortress of the Tairen in the far south.<br /><br /><i>The Dragon Reborn</i>, while not reaching the same level as <i>The Eye of the World</i>, is certainly an improvement from <i>The Great Hunt</i>. The story is more compelling, new villains arise, and the childishness, the completely unfounded arrogance and the insufferable stupidity of the main characters is finally starting to wear off. But it is <b>not</b> gone. Rand himself is barely appearing in this book, and both Mat and Nynaeve seem to be improving considerably. Perrin and Egwene, however, stand ready to assume the inglorious mantle of the worst characters.<br /><br />Mostly, though, this book is a solid addition to the story of the <i>Wheel of Time</i>, and the ending is great, leaving the reader excited for the next volume, <i>The Shadow Rising</i>.<br /><br />That's all there is to say, really. Those of you who have already read this knows what it is about. And those who haven't yet, should do so!<br /><br /><b><i>Wheel of Time reviews</i>:</b><br />#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271575" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Eye of the World</i>
</a><br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271557" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Great Hunt</i>
</a><br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271566?type=review#rating_39471354" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Dragon Reborn</i>
</a><br />#4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271584" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Shadow Rising</i>
</a><br />#5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793271654" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Fires of Heaven</i>

<div id="review_1565673531" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1565673531" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1565673531?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1565673531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16311207771183540817"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle Daily Deal 27Aug20 <a href='https://www.amazon.com/dp/B0030AF5DO/ref=s9_acsd_al_bw_c2_x_7_t?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-2&pf_rd_r=AXGRVSPKT8CYKSBT0MZ5&pf_rd_t=101&pf_rd_p=f5d64449-71e1-48e1-a21e-5c47ac0ee121&pf_rd_i=11552285011' rel='nofollow noopener'>$2.99</a></b><br/><br/>Marches buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a><br/><br/>The Dragon Reborn is my favorite book in this series so far. A few reasons for that are I’m pretty comfortable in this world now and can focus on the story more than all the parts, places and lore. The other reason is the character are becoming more developed and while at time I want to box their ears for fighting against their destiny/power/specialness so much instead of embracing it and just going with </span>
  <span id="freeText16311207771183540817" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle Daily Deal 27Aug20 <a href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B0030AF5DO/ref=s9_acsd_al_bw_c2_x_7_t?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&amp;pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-2&amp;pf_rd_r=AXGRVSPKT8CYKSBT0MZ5&amp;pf_rd_t=101&amp;pf_rd_p=f5d64449-71e1-48e1-a21e-5c47ac0ee121&amp;pf_rd_i=11552285011" rel="nofollow noopener">$2.99</a></b><br /><br />Marches buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a><br /><br />The Dragon Reborn is my favorite book in this series so far. A few reasons for that are I’m pretty comfortable in this world now and can focus on the story more than all the parts, places and lore. The other reason is the character are becoming more developed and while at time I want to box their ears for fighting against their destiny/power/specialness so much instead of embracing it and just going with it.<br /><br />Shorter review for me than normal since there are a bazillion reviews on this series. But the run down is…..<br /><br /><b>Rand</b> - Still trying to save those around him and a little lost as to what to do with himself. Also he is struggling a bit with the madness. Is he mad or is the dark one just taunting him and making him think he is starting to go mad….idk the jury is still out on that. He is on a quest to retrieve a sword that is not a sword and so even though most of his journey is shone third person a quest for a magical sword is rarely dull.<br /><br /><b>Perrin</b> - Stubborn two rivers folk. He is a wolf brother but fighting against it. (<i>see totally want to box his ears because it is so cool and I want him to explore it</i>) But we find out why it might be dangerous as well. Perrin meet a girl and damn if she doesn’t have him on his toes not knowing what to think. Let the games begin :P<br /><blockquote>
  <i> “No questions, remember? And my name is Perrin, Zarine. Not ‘big man,’ or ‘blacksmith,’ or anything else. Perrin. Perrin Aybara.”<br />“And mine is Faile, shaggy-hair.”<br />With something close to a snarl, he booted Stepper after the others. Zarine had to throw her arms around his waist to keep from being tossed over the dun’s crupper. He thought she was laughing.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Mat</b> - Well Mat has been my least favorite in prior books but he has grown a bit on me in this one. Now that he isn’t slightly crazy and paranoid he is a more likeable fellow even if he is totally oblivious to the danger surrounding him and figuring out why it is there. The Wool Headed Ox has no idea that all the trouble he has been getting into might have something to do with the Dark One or some of the forsaken. Ignorance is bliss I guess. Still he has some really interesting things going on with his new found luck and is he perhaps channeling a little bit of a king from the past…..hmmm time will tell. He is definitely a lot more interesting now.<br /><br />Mat also gets the best fight scene in this book and I totally loved how he was able to take down Elayne’s brothers with a quarterstaff. Mat is a man not to be underestimated anymore.<br /><blockquote>
  <i> “During his lifetime, Jearom fought over ten thousand times, in battle and single combat. He was defeated once. By a farmer with a quarterstaff! Remember that. Remember what you just saw.” <br />He lowered his eyes to Galad, and lowered his voice as well. “If you cannot get up by now, lad, it is finished.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Nynaeve, Egwene and Elayne</b> - These three did practically everything together in this so it is hard to separate them. Even though I got a little tired of Egwene always fighting stubbornly with Nynaeve over EVERYTHING the rest of their story arc is really interesting. Egwene’s accepted test was almost as harsh as Nynaeve’s. Also I enjoyed it as they learn more about what they can do with the one power and go on a quest to find the Black Ajah. What is revealed about the Black Ajah in this book is scary to say the least.<br /><br /><b>Best New Culture</b> - The Aiel…yes yes I know that we got a glimpse of them in the last book. But, in this one we get a better understanding of them as their culture is fleshed out. It also seems they have some prophecies of their own about the Dragon Reborn and those were some of the most interesting by far. Plus they are badass fighters.<br /><blockquote>
  <i> As if he had all the time in the world, Gaul calmly lifted a dark cloth from his shoulders and wrapped it around his head, finishing with a thick black veil that hid his face except for his eyes. <br />“Do you like to dance, Perrin Aybara?” he asked. <br />With that, he darted away from the cage. Straight at the oncoming Whitecloaks.</i>
</blockquote><br />And he totally kicked ass. But the thing I love about the Aiel is not just that the men are great fighters but also the women. They are all like ninja’s sneaking around and rarely being seen. They are masters of fighting, camouflage and stealth. Plus it seems like they might be Rand’s people and learning more about his true origins was one of the best highlights of this book for me.<br /><br /><b>Everything Else</b> - There really is a lot going on with:<br />-	some forsaken on the lose<br />-	the Black Ajah plotting<br />-	Rand’s dreams permeating those around him and the weird side effects it is causing<br />-	Loial stepping into the role of a fighter as well as an Ogier of just knowledge<br />-	Min and some of her predictions<br />-	Moraine trying to control the situation and kinda failing at it<br />-	Another prophecy coming to completion<br />-	And FINALLY maybe FINALLY Rand will accept that he IS the Dragon Reborn and not try to deny his fate or destiny any longer.<br /><br />There is definitely a lot to enjoy in this installment even if again it takes a little time to get really rolling. But overall this world and the overall plot arc is growing on me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16311207771183540817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780812513714" href="/book/show/359820.The_Dragon_Reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57392386-sam?shelf=wheel-of-time">wheel-of-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57392386-sam?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2724663893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12291947821038363031">The third chapter in the mammoth Wheel of Time saga and I’m finally starting to realise why there are fourteen books. The scope of the story Robert Jordan is weaving finally becomes evident in The Dragon Reborn.<br/><br/>After two books of Rand being the focal point of the story he is barely featured in the third installment. Instead the spotlight is directed toward Perrin and Mat, who so far have come off looking like Rand’s peripheral sidekicks.<br/><br/>Mat has finally arrived in Tar Valon to be healed of the po</span>
  <span id="freeText12291947821038363031" style="display:none">The third chapter in the mammoth Wheel of Time saga and I’m finally starting to realise why there are fourteen books. The scope of the story Robert Jordan is weaving finally becomes evident in The Dragon Reborn.<br /><br />After two books of Rand being the focal point of the story he is barely featured in the third installment. Instead the spotlight is directed toward Perrin and Mat, who so far have come off looking like Rand’s peripheral sidekicks.<br /><br />Mat has finally arrived in Tar Valon to be healed of the poison running through his body courtesy of the tainted dagger. With him are Egewene and Nynaeve who are given the task of hunting down the Black Ajah. Perrin is with Morraine and Lan on the trail of Rand who has run off seemingly on the way to Tear to take control of Callandor, the Sword of the Dragon.<br /><br />Giving Mat and Perrin time to develop as pivotal characters was a class move on the authors part. Another book solely dedicated to Rand could have turned readers against him but instead he is transformed into an insane wreck of a hero whose sparse appearances contribute to the best parts of the book.<br /><br />Mat and Perrin are able to breathe whilst away from Rand and their personalities come to the forefront as they commence their own journeys. I preferred Mat’s story over Perrin’s as he spends a greater amount of time on his own and is a more interesting character. Perrin is still slightly held back by Morraine and Lan but i’m sure he’ll venture out on his own at some point.<br /><br />Compared to The Eye of the World and The Great Hunt this is a slow burn. At around the 300 page mark i was almost regretting reading this so close after finishing The Great Hunt but suddenly the book comes to life and transforms into a work of brilliance. The ending, although expected, is still well written and worthy of a fist pumping cheer! My favourite book so far.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12291947821038363031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3355758113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3355758113" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3355758113?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/52092478-the-dragon-reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3355758113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14941916748212109647">The Dragon Reborn is the third book in the WoT series and so far the only one worth it's hype in my opinion. The plot progression and character development is at a snail's pace, it's only after three books that I finally started caring about the characters, even at that, it took me three whole months to finish this book, yes it was that uninspiring. Despite that I'll still continue this series, I'm invested now and wants to know how it all ends.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Always plan for the worst, child, that way all </i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText14941916748212109647" style="display:none">The Dragon Reborn is the third book in the WoT series and so far the only one worth it's hype in my opinion. The plot progression and character development is at a snail's pace, it's only after three books that I finally started caring about the characters, even at that, it took me three whole months to finish this book, yes it was that uninspiring. Despite that I'll still continue this series, I'm invested now and wants to know how it all ends.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Always plan for the worst, child, that way all your surprises are pleasant ones.”</i>
</b><br /><br />This picked up just where <i>The Great Hunt</i> ended with the girls on their way to Tar valon(I listened to the audiobook so my spellings of names might be incorrect). Mat was sick and Perrin finally got reunited with Rand. <br /><br />Rand still in doubt that he is actually the dragon reborn ran away so as not to hurt people he loves, Perrin and Morriane went after him. Egwene and Nynaeve were promoted to accepted at Tar valon but left shortly after on a mission. They all converge together at Tear just like the prophesy says.<br /><br /><b>
  <i><br />“If you can’t hide what you are going to do, do it so everybody thinks you are a fool.”</i>
</b><br /><br />As usual Rand is still in denial, he believes that Morriane is either wrong or trying to use him, he was barely in this and I loved that, he's PoV is always whinny and depressing.<br /><br />Nynaeve, Egwene and Elaine has lots of page space, with Nynaeve and Egwene having POVs. I really love their character development. Nynaeve still blames Morriane for ruining the lives of the Amoz fielders but she is taking it better. Egwene embraced the life of an Aes Sedai and is more willing to learn.<br /><br />Perrin is the most matured of all three boys and still is, he thinks everything through, he is still sceptical of Aes Sedai but given how he grew up it isn't surprising.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Just because fate has chosen something for you instead of you choosing it for yourself doesn’t mean it has to be bad.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Mat's character development is my favourite in this book, I disliked him in the first and second book but now I like him. He is cynical but not evil, he loves his friends and is willing to help them when in need.<br /><br />Land, Morriane and the Ogier were also in this.<br /><br />The writing though slow in progression is easy to understand, things have finally started coming together. The world building is great, but overly done. I enjoyed the fight scenes and the magic system, it's awesome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14941916748212109647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText16690509304520401523" style="display:none">3.5 to 4 stars<br /><br />Much the same as the first two.
