    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3464291761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3464291761" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3464291761?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3464291761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4919829192519550855"><i>“The breaker of bonds; the forger of chains. The maker of futures; the unshaper of destiny.”</i><br/><br/><b>Destiny is a nasty business. Rand al'Thor learns this lesson quickly. He is the Dragon Reborn, the Chosen One who will save the world... and destroy it at the same time.</b> How does somebody, who in the future is bound to succumb to the madness which will lead him to murder all the loved ones, cope with something like that? Rand is embarking on the winding path leading him to become what he is destined to be</span>
  <span id="freeText4919829192519550855" style="display:none"><i>“The breaker of bonds; the forger of chains. The maker of futures; the unshaper of destiny.”</i><br /><br /><b>Destiny is a nasty business. Rand al'Thor learns this lesson quickly. He is the Dragon Reborn, the Chosen One who will save the world... and destroy it at the same time.</b> How does somebody, who in the future is bound to succumb to the madness which will lead him to murder all the loved ones, cope with something like that? Rand is embarking on the winding path leading him to become what he is destined to become. <b>One thing is for sure: it is going to be epic.</b><br /><br />Classic high fantasy can be <b>a pleasant break from more and more realistic, dark and dirty contemporary fantasy</b>. I have read many (probably too many!) Tolkien-based series and few have been able to enchant me. By copying <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> themes, plots and tropes, Mr Jordan has created what is among the best secondary fantasy on the market because he reworked those into an original vision, maybe not equally well written, but even more epic and delivered with an even greater - in terms of page-count - panache. That alone should be appreciated. And the third volume of his series is <b>a great piece of entertainment</b>, offering everything that we love the genre for.<br /><br /><i>“Fate can kill you, if it does not do worse.”</i><br /><br /><i>Dragon Reborn</i>, as the title suggests, should focus on the main character, Rand al'Thor. Against these expectations, the Author decided on an interesting trick, namely <b>pushing the main protagonist into the margins</b>. Simultaneously, the novel brings us closer to other heroes whom we follow through the pages of the book. It was an excellent idea! I thought it very refreshing to tell a tale about the chosen one without the chosen one in attendance. I also admired how the different paths were intertwined even though half of the protagonists either wished to be elsewhere or actively planned for doing different things. In this respect, <i>Dragon Reborn</i> is largely focused on the changes that occur in them. <br /><br />Boys and girls become more and more mature, grow up into their assigned roles and face their destiny. It is neither easy nor simple. Rand’s story gives way to <b>Perrin’s</b> plot, also fleeing from his own <b>wolf dreams</b> and the insanity they bring with them, and <b>Mat’s, who turns out to be one of the most interesting characters and who definitely gains in this volume</b> (in the previous volumes he irritated rather than aroused my sympathy). Those POVs are both interesting and addictive, but the plot of <b>Egwene and BFF squad becomes unbearable with time. These girls are too full of themselves and essentially ungrateful wretches</b>, and I shudder to think what is going to happen when the inevitable romance kicks in. <br /><br /><i>“Everywhere I go, you humans are doing things, hurrying and scurrying, having things happen to you. How can you stand so much excitement?”</i><br /><br />As we accompany the heroes more or less consciously race against time, and against each other, it can be frustrating at times. The <b>reader knows far more than the protagonists so s/he can grow exasperated as they flail about blind and unsuspecting, not seeing the larger picture we are privy to</b>. Mr Jordan shows once again how important the dreams are. It is not only an opportunity to predict the future or to confront one’s subconsciousness. The things experienced in dreams have real effects in reality. The <b>dream sequences are superb and rival to the ones in Harry Potter</b>, which I always thought exquisite. <br /><br />There are more and more strange events and inexplicable phenomena in the world, which clearly indicate that seals are binding Ba’alzamon and his minions are weakening. There are, of course, the ubiquitous conspiracies, plots, more or less particular interests that influence the direction in which the world turns. And it is this world, represented by its wealth of histories, lands, peoples and their customs, that is perhaps the greatest asset of the series. I was especially fascinated by the Aiel, who to my delight play an increasingly important role.<br /><br /><i>“If events outrun me, they may well trample you, and the rest of the world with you.”</i> <br /><br />This is definitely <b>the best book in the series so far</b> and it draws the reader in even more than the previous two, which were really good. For me, <i>Dragon Reborn</i> reads much better than <i>The Great Hunt</i> as I am not able to indicate any moment of boredom, and there were those in the previous instalment. And yes, I know people complained that the ending is rushed. But really, that was <b>an Erikson-worthy convergence written even before Erikson learnt what a trope is</b>. There are two things I would like to point out with regard to the grand finale. <br /><br />Firstly, some of you might know my unholy obsession with the <i>Malazan Book of the Fallen</i>. Malazan, if you have read the series, you will know that, is basically wholly built on the premise of the convergence. This concept has been a backbone of everything that happens in every single book and the whole series as a whole. In Malazan, I have seen some far-fetched and miraculous endings. In comparison, just the fact that the final chapter of <i>Dragon Reborn</i> has a kind of mission impossible, last-minute, perfectly timed sequence is not <i>that</i> galling.<br /><br />Secondly, it is worth remembering that <b>we are only at the beginning of the road. This book is the culmination of a very extensive introduction.</b> As I was finishing the last page, I basically realised that <i>“This is just the beginning,”</i> and that there are actually a dozen or so volumes ahead of me. It would be silly to expect an ultimate climax from something that was, in fact, a three-volume long prologue. <br /><br />And what a prologue it was! Now, to the series proper.<br /><br />Also in the series: <br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1592464110?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eye of the World</a> ★★★★☆<br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3269109635" rel="nofollow noopener">The Great Hunt</a> ★★★★☆<br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3645853871" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow Rising</a> ★★★★☆<br />5. The Fires of Heaven RTC<br />6. Lord of Chaos RTC<br />7. A Crown of Swords RTC <br />8. The Path of Daggers RTC<br />9. Winter’s Heart RTC<br />10. Crossroads of Twighlight RTC<br />11. Knife of Dreams RTC<br />12. The Gathering Storm RTC <br />13. Towers of Midnight RTC<br />14. A Memory of Light RTC</span>
  <a data-text-id="4919829192519550855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313285545" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/313285545?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313285545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14139631429631249635">Like the first couple of WoT books The Dragon Reborn started a little slow and then developed into quite an engaging and exciting read. I like Jordan's storytelling style. He manages to keep me interested in the characters and the happenings even when not a lot is actually happening! <br/><br/>Despite being titled The Dragon Reborn this book was notable for the distinct absence of Rand as a POV character. That meant that Perrin, Egwene, and Mat had to pick up the slack. It was the making of both Mat and P</span>
  <span id="freeText14139631429631249635" style="display:none">Like the first couple of WoT books The Dragon Reborn started a little slow and then developed into quite an engaging and exciting read. I like Jordan's storytelling style. He manages to keep me interested in the characters and the happenings even when not a lot is actually happening! <br /><br />Despite being titled The Dragon Reborn this book was notable for the distinct absence of Rand as a POV character. That meant that Perrin, Egwene, and Mat had to pick up the slack. It was the making of both Mat and Perrin as both have now developed nicely as characters. Mat was a little annoying in the early stages before stealing the show in the second half of the book. Perrin is now just dependably likeable and interesting. Things went less well for Egwene. Her story was interesting, but she herself has gotten a bit less likeable. <br /><br />The world building was as awesome as ever and we got to visit more places, like Illian and Tear, in this instalment. We also got to learn a bit more about the White Cloaks and the Forsaken! <br /><br />Jordan wove a bunch of interesting story arc over the course of the story and then had a lot of those separate threads converge in an explosive and exciting ending. <br /><br />All in all this was a great addition to the WoT series.<br /><br />Rating: 4.5 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note. Krammer and Reading were fantastic as always. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14139631429631249635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8153990-the-dragon-reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42952572-miche?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42952572-miche?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137264470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9555307889148498337">2.5 stars.<br/><br/>So far I struggled with all books I read from this series. I normally enjoy journey books, but the ones from Wheel of Time might be the exception. <br/><br/>The plot development at this installment moved at snail speed. The last 15% of this book was nice, but it wasn't worth the time I had to spend reading the other 85% about inn descriptions, skirts smoothed, braids tugged and dice tossed. The constant repetition during most of the book had me wondering how this book passed the edition phase.<br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText9555307889148498337" style="display:none">2.5 stars.<br /><br />So far I struggled with all books I read from this series. I normally enjoy journey books, but the ones from Wheel of Time might be the exception. <br /><br />The plot development at this installment moved at snail speed. The last 15% of this book was nice, but it wasn't worth the time I had to spend reading the other 85% about inn descriptions, skirts smoothed, braids tugged and dice tossed. The constant repetition during most of the book had me wondering how this book passed the edition phase.<br /><br />There are some points that I liked:<br /><br />-Matt's character development was really well handled. He was the one I couldn't stand at the previous two books and he became one of my favorite characters by the end of this book.<br /><br />-The Aiel. Such an interesting people!<br /><br />-Perrin's arc was slow, but interesting nonetheless.<br /><br />Overall it wasn't a bad book. A lot of people enjoyed, as you can see by all the 5 and 4 stars reviews. However, I when I finished this book, the only feeling I had was one of wasting time in a underwhelming journey.<br /><br />I might try the next book as I was told that it is one of the best in the series. If that one doesn't grab by attention, it will be my farewell to the Wheel of Time.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14701355498822372385">This is one where they walk a lot.<br/><br/>No mention of plot, since this is the third book in a fourteen book series, and I'd hate to spoil anyone. <br/><br/>This is classical fantasy at its best, and possibly also classical fantasy at its most descriptive.   <span id="freeText14701355498822372385" style="display:none">This is one where they walk a lot.<br /><br />No mention of plot, since this is the third book in a fourteen book series, and I'd hate to spoil anyone. <br /><br />This is classical fantasy at its best, and possibly also classical fantasy at its most descriptive. I highly enjoy these books, but they take me a long time to read. I'm not the biggest fan of descriptive prose, and don't feel the need to find out about every character's clothing in detail.<br /><br />It took me a while to get into this one. A surprise, since this is the third one, but I felt like plot-wise not a lot happened for the first 60% but then I couldn't put it down during the last few hundred pages.<br /><br />Also, thank you, to whoever pointed out braid tugging to me, now I can't help but notice just how often Jordan's women randomly tug on their braids.</span>

<div id="review_494050801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/494050801" />
    <a title="Liam Degnan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan"><img alt="Liam Degnan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/494050801?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam Degnan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam Degnan" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan">Liam Degnan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765334350" href="/book/show/13513484-the-dragon-reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180038-liam-degnan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer494050801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9144159716747635041"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“We rode on the winds of the rising storm,<br/>We ran to the sounds of the thunder.<br/>We danced among the lightning bolts,<br/>and tore the world asunder.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b> <br/><b>
  <u>4.5 Stars: ✰✰✰✰½</u>
</b><br/><br/>Been falling a tad behind on my review-writing haha, but I always catch up =]. My reviews from this point out might get somewhat shorter, because the deeper you go into a series (especially one so long as this), the harder it is to write full-length reviews without spoilers. Unless I have something exceptionally good, or ex</span>
  <span id="freeText9144159716747635041" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“We rode on the winds of the rising storm,<br />We ran to the sounds of the thunder.<br />We danced among the lightning bolts,<br />and tore the world asunder.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b> <br /><b>
  <u>4.5 Stars: ✰✰✰✰½</u>
</b><br /><br />Been falling a tad behind on my review-writing haha, but I always catch up =]. My reviews from this point out might get somewhat shorter, because the deeper you go into a series (especially one so long as this), the harder it is to write full-length reviews without spoilers. Unless I have something exceptionally good, or exceptionally bad to rant about, of course ;]. <br /><br />This was another truly excellent installment in a series that grows on me more and more. Not quite as good at it's predecessor, but where that book focused a great deal on developing the story and world, <b>this book commits a good bit of time towards developing the characters</b>, and this was much needed. We have fewer developments in the worldbuilding and the plot, but we gain a lot of traction in the lives of the individual characters, and this was an excellent decision on Jordan's part. <br /><br />Actually, he made a lot of really smart decisions in this book, I thought. <b>Number One best decision by far was moving Rand into the background of the story for this book, and focusing on our other Emond's Fielders</b>. This was essential if the other characters were going to become meaningful parts of the story. Perrin, Egwene, and Mat each get A LOT of air time in this book, making for a pretty big shift in the narrative, but I actually loved it. Perrin has been my favorite character since book one, even though he had very little air time in book two, so I loved getting to see him come more into his own in this book, and the same thing goes for Mat and Egwene. <br /><br /><b>The characters in this series just keep getting better, honestly</b>. It's a slow-burn though. I think of my experience with Mistborn, where my love for the characters was almost instantaneous, and the development of each character was done pretty quickly. It's not like that in this series. Jordan takes his time, but this makes for something special in it's own way, because you really get to see the gradual growth and progression of each character over time. It's really pretty cool.<br /><br /><b>The Worldbuilding was dialed back significantly in this book though, as a result</b>. We see much less of the different cultures, a significantly smaller number of POVs in comparison to The Great Hunt, the plot of this book was not nearly as multi-layered as the last, and <b>there really weren't any villains in this book that stood out to me</b>. The Great Hunt literally blew me away in this capacity, while this book was good, but not exceptional. Again, this isn't a bad thing in regards to the series as a whole, because the attention was needed elsewhere. I say this just as something to keep in mind =]. <br /><br /><b>And now, for my one problem, and probably the only reason I took off half a star</b>. I hate formulas. What I mean by "formulas" is that when you pick up a certain book, you know how it's going to start and how it's going to end before you even read the back cover. The last three books have had what feels like an almost identical ending, closely following what feels like the same pattern. Spoiler for those who have read these: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It seems like Rand has an epic show-down with the Dark Lord at the end of every book, wins, and then realizes after that the Dark Lord is still alive. I'm hoping that this doesn't happen again in book four, because it's starting to become repetitive <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It's not like a huge deal, and some might disagree, but I can see myself getting tired of the repetition. I'm in book four now, so I'll have to wait and see =]. <br /><br />Overall though, <b>I have thoroughly enjoyed reading these books</b>. I basically inhaled this one over the course of three days, and picked up book four immediately after, so in spite of my one or two quibbles I can't emphasize enough how excellent this series has been so far. Great characters, amazing worldbuilding, and an excellent story. Beyond that, all of the positive things I've mentioned in my previous reviews still apply to this one, so check those out if you're interested =]. I can't wait to continue!<br /><br />Happy reading =]. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Just because fate has chosen something for you instead of you choosing it for yourself doesn’t mean it has to be bad. Even if it’s something you are sure you would never have chosen in a hundred years."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9144159716747635041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2040717512" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2040717512" />
    <a title="Angus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35418511-angus"><img alt="Angus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588262898p2/35418511.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2040717512?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angus" href="/user/show/35418511-angus">Angus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780812513714" href="/book/show/359820.The_Dragon_Reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35418511-angus?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2040717512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15907069332972662159">I don't think I have ever been this invested in a series before and i'm so happy! I understand some people's reasoning for not liking The Wheel of Time, as yes... it's filled with a lot of cliches and tropes (at least in the first book) However, I just happen to love each and every one of these tropes! While I'm glad more modern fantasy has developed and become more original, I just find it so refreshing to go back to the genre at its core and this series just makes me so happy for them reasons </span>
  <span id="freeText15907069332972662159" style="display:none">I don't think I have ever been this invested in a series before and i'm so happy! I understand some people's reasoning for not liking The Wheel of Time, as yes... it's filled with a lot of cliches and tropes (at least in the first book) However, I just happen to love each and every one of these tropes! While I'm glad more modern fantasy has developed and become more original, I just find it so refreshing to go back to the genre at its core and this series just makes me so happy for them reasons :D <br /><br />The Dragon Reborn is actually my favourite book so far and this is why... <br /><br />In this installment, there is much less POV time for Rand and I actually think this does wonders for the series, as it allows every other character and plot line to develop massively. For example, I feel as though the female characters really come into their own in this book and become their own individual person with their own distinct personalities. Whereas previously I couldn't help but get confused between Egwene and Nynaeve, as I didn't think there was much separating them. While they are still not my favourite characters in the series, I absolutely loved their scenes in this book as they reminded me so much of why I love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13497.A_Feast_for_Crows__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___4_" title="A Feast for Crows (A Song of Ice and Fire, #4) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Feast for Crows</a>, due to all the <br />slowly built up secrecy and court intrigue! (but the White Tower version)<br /><br />We also get more Perrin, who is my favourite of the 3 Edmond's Field boys! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(I may have a slight obsession with wolves) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I also started to really grow towards Mat in this book, as he became so much more entertaining to read about and not annoying in the slightest! I also loved Queen Morgase, as she reminds me of Queen Elizabeth 1 crossed with the Queen of Hearts and it just makes me laugh xD I also found Lanfear incredibly interesting as a character and can't wait to learn more about her and her motives! <br /><br />But what really made this book my favourite in the series so far was the pacing and how it was structured. The pacing was consistently on the increase and slowly built up to an epic climax that definitely satisfies! Also we stayed with one character enough to really develop the story arc before switching POV, instead of switching every other chapter, which can sometimes be quite jarring as in other fantasy books. And then to top it off plot points from the previous two books come back into play and it's just.... *claps* Well played Mr Jordan well played. <br /><br />I absolutely love this series and I am so glad there are still 11 books to go! All it needs now is a circus and my life is complete! XD <br /><br />Spoiler alert- Nynaeve tugs her braid</span>
  <a data-text-id="15907069332972662159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3287733233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3287733233" />
    <a title="Valliya Rennell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58882300-valliya-rennell"><img alt="Valliya Rennell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596694907p2/58882300.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3287733233?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valliya Rennell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valliya Rennell" href="/user/show/58882300-valliya-rennell">Valliya Rennell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8153990-the-dragon-reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=d-fantasy">d-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=x-reviewed-books">x-reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58882300-valliya-rennell?shelf=a-3-stars">a-3-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3287733233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1263820185302603903">3 stars<br/><i>**Although this is a spoiler free review (spoilers are hidden), there may be spoilers for previous books in the series (scroll down)**</i><br/><br/><b>*braid-tugging intensifies**</b> After finishing <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233649.The_Great_Hunt__The_Wheel_of_Time___2_' title='The Great Hunt (The Wheel of Time, #2) by Robert Jordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Great Hunt</a>, I was dying to get into this. The ending wit the Battle of Falme, the blowing of the Horn, the Seachan, oh it was so perfect. I could not wait to see where the follow up would take me because WOW I felt exhilarated and hyped up. Although I still think <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34897.The_Dragon_Reborn__The_Wheel_of_Time___3_' title='The Dragon Reborn (The Wheel of Time, #3) by Robert Jordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dragon Reborn</a> is a<b> good novel, but compare</b></span>
  <span id="freeText1263820185302603903" style="display:none">3 stars<br><i>**Although this is a spoiler free review (spoilers are hidden), there may be spoilers for previous books in the series (scroll down)**</i><br><br><b>*braid-tugging intensifies**</b> After finishing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233649.The_Great_Hunt__The_Wheel_of_Time___2_" title="The Great Hunt (The Wheel of Time, #2) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Great Hunt</a>, I was dying to get into this. The ending wit the Battle of Falme, the blowing of the Horn, the Seachan, oh it was so perfect. I could not wait to see where the follow up would take me because WOW I felt exhilarated and hyped up. Although I still think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34897.The_Dragon_Reborn__The_Wheel_of_Time___3_" title="The Dragon Reborn (The Wheel of Time, #3) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dragon Reborn</a> is a<b> good novel, but compared to its predecessors, it shines a little weaker.</b> After a hard winter, following the events on Almoth Plain, Rand, Perrin, Lan, Min and the Shienar company camp in the mountains waiting for a good time to proceed with Moiraine's plans for Rand as the Dragon reborn. <b>Rand, though, is going through a mental breakdown not knowing if he really is the Dragon, or just the Aes Sedais' puppet. </b>When he runs off to Tear in the attempts to raise the great sword Callandor and prove to himself if he really is the Dragon, Perrin, Lan, Moiraine and company soon follow in pursuit. What they find in Rand's wake is a path of very peculiar occurrences. On the other hand, Elayne, Nynaeve, Egwene, Verin, and Mat finally make it back to Tar Valon to get Mat healed and separated from the Shadar Logoth dagger. What the three young novices/Accepted find, though, is a <b>Tower in shambles crawling with Soulless and terrifyingly, Black Ajah</b>. As new weaves in the Pattern are formed, events all start tumbling down to a<b> final showdown</b>... but what will happen then?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Always plan for the worst, child, that way all your surprises are pleasant ones."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I really should have listened to Verin when she said this. Again, not that I disliked this book, compared to many it is still good, but I think I set my expectations way too high. I know this is a very controversial opinion as I heard many people proclaiming that this is where <i>The Wheel of Time</i> gets phenomenal. It didn't for me. <b>I felt like all our Two Rivers gang decided to channel Tobey Maguire in Spiderman 3:</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591203589ra/29589152.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Rand in the last book was losing it. Sure. But when this book begins he is in full on brooding-emo mode. I did not like this. Later on he also does some pretty shady stuff that I felt totally distanced us from what I came to love about him in book 2. He doesn't get that much screen time in this book. Maybe a total of 50-pages (POV-wise). Perrin and Egwene both started having intense anger issues. Perrin, sure I understand what spending 6-months in the mountains alone feels like... It's quarantine after all, but<b> Egwene?? She just turns so anti-everyone. If she lived now she'd probably go through a goth phase while silently making heart eyes at Galad and posting on Instagram fake-deep quotes.</b> As for Perrin, he just kinda seems to go through a rebellious teen phase, Moiraine and Lan being his parents. I wasn't really into that. Nynaeve tries to hold it together but OHHHH MAN she really has to get that braid tugging together. Mat in the beginning is a whiny twat. I know he is frustrated, but darn, I just couldn't take it. <b>The Mat situation really did start improving later on and I am starting to see why so many people love him. </b>He just isn't at that point for me yet.<br><br>Overall, Jordan really did stick the landing in the end. I had shivers. Great ending that really made up for most of my frustrations along the way. I hate to compare this once again to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233649.The_Great_Hunt__The_Wheel_of_Time___2_" title="The Great Hunt (The Wheel of Time, #2) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Great Hunt</a>, but I gotta. The reason I don't think I loved it as much as I could have is because this book <b>follows almost the exact same formula as book 2</b>. I did not like that at all. Once again the party is separated just to accidentally form up in the end for a battle. Variation was needed. And the execution wasn't as good as in book 2.  I hated that the Tar Valon squad kept getting caught. They are so powerful, yet so utterly helpless. Not gonna lie, it got on my nerves a tad. At the end of book 2 Egwene was caught by the Seanchan, at the end of book 3, all of them are caught by Be'lal. Come on! In book 2 there is a huge showdown with a spectacular army brought on by the Horn of Valere. Now there is an army of Aiel fighting alongside the People of the Dragon. Rand and Ba'alzamon have an intense fight in book 2 and in book 3, but this time it is more confusing. Still a good ending, but a bit formulaic and less fun. I really hope that the next book in the series varies up the formula a bit.<b> This one was so similar to book 2 but without the intrigue, and less wonder than book 1. Still good though.</b><br><br>Looking forward to book 4, I cannot wait to find out more about the Aiel. If we will follow the prophecies, that means that we are journeying to the Three Fold Land. Can't wait. The Aiel culture holds a lot of promise, so I really want to spend more time exploring it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34897.The_Dragon_Reborn__The_Wheel_of_Time___3_" title="The Dragon Reborn (The Wheel of Time, #3) by Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dragon Reborn</a> is a solid book but a tad formulaic... kinda like the<b> emo version of its predecessor.</b><br><br>-----------------------------------<br><i><u>Books in series</u></i>:<br>#0 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3618755763" rel="nofollow noopener">New Spring</a>: ★★.75 <br>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3208850047" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eye of the World</a>: ★★★.5 <br>#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3243314516" rel="nofollow noopener">The Great Hunt</a>: ★★★.75<br>#3 The Dragon Reborn: ★★★<br>#4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3396516141" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow Rising</a>: ★★★★.25<br>#5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3535966517" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fires of Heaven</a>: ★★★★</span>
  <a data-text-id="1263820185302603903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_381019199" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381019199" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381019199?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781429960168" href="/book/show/7361459-the-dragon-reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381019199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9847581678191815530">The prophesies of the Dragon Reborn must be fulfilled, including the one about the sword which is not a sword. The Dark One still hunts three boys from the Two Rivers in their dreams and in reality. The aftermath of the events in the end of the previous book sends disturbance waves throughout the whole land. <br/><br/>Unlike the previous book, this one has Rand's POV for about 10 pages total; now it is his turn to take a backseat for Perrin and Mat as well as wonder girls (Nynaeve, Egwene, and Elaine). Ma</span>
  <span id="freeText9847581678191815530" style="display:none">The prophesies of the Dragon Reborn must be fulfilled, including the one about the sword which is not a sword. The Dark One still hunts three boys from the Two Rivers in their dreams and in reality. The aftermath of the events in the end of the previous book sends disturbance waves throughout the whole land. <br /><br />Unlike the previous book, this one has Rand's POV for about 10 pages total; now it is his turn to take a backseat for Perrin and Mat as well as wonder girls (Nynaeve, Egwene, and Elaine). Mat finally gets his own POV and it quickly becomes one of the most interesting in the book and stays that way throughout the series consistently - there is a reason why his name often pops up in the lists of the best fantasy characters ever. Have you ever wondered while playing an RPG game - computer or pen-and-paper - what it means when you get an artifact with luck +1? Read Mat's parts of the book to find out. <br /><br />Perrin's plot line is interesting, but not too big here. He also gets to meet the most annoying character in the series later on. The most intriguing part is to see how Min's obscure predictions about him come to life.<br /><br />The wonder girls come back to Tar Valon to continue their interrupted training. It turns out, the White Tower where the training takes place is extremely dangerous place; from my personal impression I would feel much safer in the Great Blight (the stronghold of the bad guys). As a result, the girls' training became much lesser priority for them then to stay alive. <br /><br />This book is considered by many to be the classic of genre (along with two previous and two following ones) and is a must-read for any fantasy fan; 5 solid stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9847581678191815530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_298659690" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/298659690" />
    <a title="Mpauli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8323869-mpauli"><img alt="Mpauli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373482375p2/8323869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/298659690?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mpauli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mpauli" href="/user/show/8323869-mpauli">Mpauli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8153990-the-dragon-reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=genre_fantasy">genre_fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8323869-mpauli?shelf=genre_epic-fantasy">genre_epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer298659690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13071805471827206661">I think my journey to finally get to the Wheel of Time is almost as long as the series itself. I was recommended that series in the mid 90s by a friend and bought the first 8-10 books in German (in Germany, due to 1000 english words roughly being 1500 German words, books are often split in two halves) and read the first 3, which would be The Eye of the World and half of The Great Hunt.<br/>As the books seemed very slow, especially for my action-craving younger self (waves to the past) I moved on to o</span>
  <span id="freeText13071805471827206661" style="display:none">I think my journey to finally get to the Wheel of Time is almost as long as the series itself. I was recommended that series in the mid 90s by a friend and bought the first 8-10 books in German (in Germany, due to 1000 english words roughly being 1500 German words, books are often split in two halves) and read the first 3, which would be The Eye of the World and half of The Great Hunt.<br />As the books seemed very slow, especially for my action-craving younger self (waves to the past) I moved on to other things and never returned.<br />In 2006 I rediscovered the series, bought a box-set of the first 3, read The Eye of the World and never continued.<br />Finally around 2013 or 14 when the whole Sanderson hype started out, I re-read Eye of the World for the 3rd time, waited for another 2-3 years and read The Great Hunt and now finally got to The Dragon Reborn.<br /><br />That is a very long introduction just to show you why actually finishing and 4 starring (previous two books were 3 stars for me) is actually a big deal, because this time around I really have the urge to continue and tackle the Wheel of Time for good.<br /><br />I think I have adjusted to Jordan's writing and now better understand what to expect, so I'm not that annoyed by the umpteenth innkeep or most of the characters behaving headstrongly dumb in a lot of the conversations.<br />I adapted and actually enjoyed this one quite a bit, despite not much happening. Rand wasn't really in that book, although he played a pivotal role and we actually see a lot more of Mat, Perryn, Egwene, Nynave and Elayne.<br />This is actually a gutsy decision for a novel series that follows some very classical plot routes of "boy with a destiny against a dark lord".<br /><br />Overall I cherished the scenic road this time, tried to dig into the mysteries and prophcies and learnt more about some different towns, cultures and factions. <br />And now I'm interested to find out what will happen to those characters (I have 2-3 wild theories) and what the hell will be the content of another 11 books in that series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13071805471827206661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_40148362" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40148362" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40148362?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40148362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer143323156092120185">I'm continuing my reread, in preparation for next year's grand finale, but I'm sorry to have gotten a bit behind in my reviews.<br/><br/>It's crazy to think that the events from this book, book 3 in the Wheel of Time, The Dragon Reborn [US] [UK], were actually supposed to be the conclusion to the first book in the trilogy. With that in mind, it's not too hard to fathom how things have come to be. This is a turn off for a lot of people, but really, you can't go wrong with more is better, not with The Wheel</span>
  <span id="freeText143323156092120185" style="display:none">I'm continuing my reread, in preparation for next year's grand finale, but I'm sorry to have gotten a bit behind in my reviews.<br /><br />It's crazy to think that the events from this book, book 3 in the Wheel of Time, The Dragon Reborn [US] [UK], were actually supposed to be the conclusion to the first book in the trilogy. With that in mind, it's not too hard to fathom how things have come to be. This is a turn off for a lot of people, but really, you can't go wrong with more is better, not with The Wheel of Time. (We'll see if my mind ever changes in this regard).<br /><br />The Dragon Reborn was a frustrating book for me the first time around. I obviously didn't know what I was getting myself into the first time did I? :) It really drove me crazy that the main protagonist, THE Dragon Reborn, hardly makes 3 pages worth of an appearance in his own named book. The main character who actually moves this series forward is off in la-la land for the majority of the book. How does that even happen?!?!<br /><br />And then Rand is what is featured on the cover of the new ebook. Cracks me up, just a bit. The Sweet cover makes sense on the first one, it being a pretty big event, but I really don't get the ebook. What about Perrin or Mat or Egwene, Elayne, Nynaeve... so many more could make such a better cover.<br /><br />To top it all off, I actually didn't even really like Mat the first time through. Who does that? I think I really just wanted to see the next thing to happen and in the Wheel of Time, you have to be in it for the long run, you have to want to know everything about everyone. I think I'm there... finally.<br /><br />On reread, it's a whole new ballgame. I've not only grown to enjoy the other characters much more, but it's a good possibility that I like them even more than I do Rand. Learning about their story arcs, their impressions, their place in the grand scheme of things was really fun and I can't wait to see what huge roles they will play in the end. Let's be honest here, there's no way Rand can handle everything on his own. He can't even handle the brewing love triangle.<br /><br />I've been trying to include a description of each of the books in every review, but I can't really get myself to do this anymore when such a better one can be found at Tor.com, viewed here.<br /><br />I make a lot of jokes about this series, but it's all in good fun. There are very few books I love as much as The Wheel of Time.<br /><br />5 out of 5 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="143323156092120185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_453850060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/453850060" />
    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11665678-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362814696p2/11665678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/453850060?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/11665678-kyle">Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer453850060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7550619301144422263">The Wheel of Time series represents, for me, the perfect example of a guilty pleasure in the world of fantasy.<br/><br/>This series is not actually written very well. Robert Jordan was not a very good wordsmith, and he really only knew how to say and describe things one way. His characters are generally unbelievable, and have ridiculous dialogue. The plot is tremendously predictable, and is heavily influenced (close to the point of being unoriginal) by the fantasy works that came before. The whole story i</span>
  <span id="freeText7550619301144422263" style="display:none">The Wheel of Time series represents, for me, the perfect example of a guilty pleasure in the world of fantasy.<br /><br />This series is not actually written very well. Robert Jordan was not a very good wordsmith, and he really only knew how to say and describe things one way. His characters are generally unbelievable, and have ridiculous dialogue. The plot is tremendously predictable, and is heavily influenced (close to the point of being unoriginal) by the fantasy works that came before. The whole story is much, much longer than it needs to be and obviously became bigger than Jordan could handle.<br /><br />That being said... I still enjoy these books. I can't rationally explain it, and I've re-read most of them at least a couple times. I shouldn't be so attached to them, yet I'm chained by my own embarrassed desire to periodically dive into the wheel of time. The only explanation I can think of, is that Jordan was a wizard. Not a skillful, subtle, thoughtful wizard; a sneaky, dark, and soul-sucking wizard who has enchanted me by his mediocre writing.<br /><br />Many people despise and look down their nose at these books, and I totally understand that. Many people also love and adore these books, and will forever place The Wheel of Time series upon their list of all-time favorite books. I can understand that impulse too.<br />I realize this review is lacking in helpfulness, but the important thing to take away is this: try these books out. If you hate them, then fine. At least you'll have given them a chance. If you Love them, then great! Good for you, and you have a long, LONG, journey ahead of you filled with something you love. Either way, you'll have exposed yourself to one of the most famous fantasy series of all time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7550619301144422263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2551067961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2551067961" />
    <a title="Zitong Ren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77983193-zitong-ren"><img alt="Zitong Ren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552188473p2/77983193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2551067961?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zitong Ren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zitong Ren" href="/user/show/77983193-zitong-ren">Zitong Ren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780812513714" href="/book/show/359820.The_Dragon_Reborn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=epics">epics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=contains-romance">contains-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2551067961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9269699257283626352">So, this was great. It naturally featured a load of braid tugging from Nynaeve, but that was to be expected. This review is written after had reread it, so it is written in the lens of someone who knows what is going to happen later down the track. Now, as I did go through this novel, there were so many things that I had forgotten and to be honest, most of the middle books have sort of just blended together in my brain. I actually completely forgot that Aviendha showed up this early and although</span>
  <span id="freeText9269699257283626352" style="display:none">So, this was great. It naturally featured a load of braid tugging from Nynaeve, but that was to be expected. This review is written after had reread it, so it is written in the lens of someone who knows what is going to happen later down the track. Now, as I did go through this novel, there were so many things that I had forgotten and to be honest, most of the middle books have sort of just blended together in my brain. I actually completely forgot that Aviendha showed up this early and although her role was limited, imagine my surprise about half-way through this book. Before I started this novel, I was also wondering as to if Faile was going to appear in this novel or the next, and hey, it was this one. <br /><br />I find it interesting that in the first few books, the plot actual does progress at a steady pace with one or two major events happening at the end of every book. While there it a fair amount of travelling in this novel, the plot does also progress a fair chunk and loads of interesting things happen. I’m aware that even in the earlier books people complain of it being slow, not to mention how it gets much worse during the ‘slog’ books, but I actually don’t mind at the amount of plot progression we received. For me, this is really a book series, where every moment is to be savoured and that it is meant to be slow, considering all of the worldbuilding and detail that goes into it.<br /><br />The worldbuilding in this world genuinely fantastic and everything is so rich, layered and detailed. Now, I wouldn’t want all of my fantasy to be this full, but considering that this is a monstrous fourteen books series, it really needed the level of worldbuilding that is present. The map sort of looks a bit dodgy/sort of boring in that it is just one big land mass, but it doesn’t really bother me too much and the actual history behind is done really well even though the completely straight lines of mountain ranges is not really geographically feasible. <br /><br />Despite the Wheel of Time being one of my favourite series ever, largely for it just being such exceptional fantasy, there are also plenty of flaws. This is very much so an incredibly slow series and many people will want much more things to be moving forward. The reason I don’t really mind this is that I love the world so that any moment I’m spending in it is just such a joy. Another thing, the romances in this novel are largely all pretty bad and there are many instances of instalove, or near instalove. I actually think many of the characters have decent chemistry between each other(not all do) and they normally work out ok in the end, but the speed at which characters seem to be in love which each other, wowee do some of these relationships happen quickly. Surprisingly liked the relationship between Faile and Perrin and they had sort of decent chemistry together for a relationship in the Wheel of Time. As a fan, I’m aware of its flaws and it hardly is for everyone, but I still really loved this book, nonetheless.<br /><br />I suppose one thing I would have liked was a bit more payoff at the end. While the ending was monumental in what did happen, it was also sort of over fairly quickly, yet at the same time, all the books are all really just building up towards the final book so it is understandable. <br /><br />Even though Jordan’s romances is one of his weakest spots, he really excels at writing character. Some of these characters, and their arcs throughout the entire series are just amazing. Mat Cauthon for me is just such a great character with so much personality and despite all of the braid tugging, I really do love Nynaeve’s character as well and her development is just fantastic. Rand barely appears in this book, so I won’t comment to much on him, but I find him to be interesting if nothing else. Moiraine is simply fantastic as always and I was so glad to see other prominent characters in the series start popping up in this book. <br /><br />I’m surprised Nynaeve’s braid hasn’t been pulled apart yet and it is only book three, but that is The Wheel of Time. 9/10</span>
  <a data-text-id="9269699257283626352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14837000756957070019" style="display:none">"The Wheel of Time turns, and Ages come and pass, leaving memories that become legend.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X4pHGJ7+ZhZOlR3TCBjODnKCX8STr+PVvodmJDzmhBRtuhDXZIT8mI8zX6O7xWl3kkJ3IefYhRcH57UOYkY3og==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cD1Mn7ebwAYsuVJjJbPwRRnpAr5DlA5ZoPlhFMJP5N1CDRtQTeFaiO0fEBOWblc8+SkqWzfjaJsZmbI+nO9Xaw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7439792368939665259"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Robert Jordan was the pen name of James Oliver Rigney, Jr., under which he was best known as the author of the bestselling The Wheel of Time fantasy series. He also wrote under the names <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108933.Reagan_O_Neal' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reagan O'Neal</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/943931.Jackson_O_Reilly' title='Jackson O'Reilly' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jackson O'Reilly</a>.<br/><br/>Jordan was born in Charleston, South Carolina. He served two tours in Vietnam (from 1968 to</span>
  <span id="freeText7439792368939665259" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br />Robert Jordan was the pen name of James Oliver Rigney, Jr., under which he was best known as the author of the bestselling The Wheel of Time fantasy series. He also wrote under the names <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108933.Reagan_O_Neal" rel="nofollow noopener">Reagan O'Neal</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/943931.Jackson_O_Reilly" title="Jackson O'Reilly" rel="nofollow noopener">Jackson O'Reilly</a>.<br /><br />Jordan was born in Charleston, South Carolina. He served two tours in Vietnam (from 1968 to 1970) with the United States Army as a helicopter gunner. He was awarded the Distinguished Flying Cross with bronze oak leaf cluster, the Bronze Star with "V" and bronze oak leaf cluster, and two Vietnamese Gallantry Crosses with palm. After returning from Vietnam he attended The Citadel where he received an undergraduate degree in physics. After graduating he was employed by the United States Navy as a nuclear engineer. He began writing in 1977. He was a history buff and enjoyed hunting, fishing, sailing, poker, chess, pool, and pipe collecting. <br /><br />He described himself as a "High Church" Episcopalian and received communion more than once a week. He lived with his wife Harriet McDougal, who works as a book editor (currently with Tor Books; she was also Jordan's editor) in a house built in 1797. <br /><br />Responding to queries on the similarity of some of the concepts in his Wheel of Time books with Freemasonry concepts, Jordan admitted that he was a Freemason. However, "like his father and grandfather," he preferred not to advertise, possibly because of the negative propaganda against Freemasonry. In his own words, "no man in this country should feel in danger because of his beliefs."<br /><br />On March 23, 2006, Jordan disclosed in a statement that he had been diagnosed with cardiac amyloidosis, and that with treatment, his median life expectancy was four years, though he said he intended to beat the statistics. He later posted on his Dragonmount blog to encourage his fans not to worry about him and that he intended to have a long and fully creative life.<br /><br />He began chemotherapy treatment at Mayo Clinic in Rochester, Minnesota, in early April 2006. Jordan was enrolled in a study using the drug Revlimid just approved for multiple myeloma but not yet tested on primary amyloidosis.<br /><br />Jordan died at approximately 2:45 p.m. EDT on September 16, 2007, and a funeral service was held for him on Wednesday, September 19, 2007. Jordan was cremated and his ashes buried in the churchyard of St. James Church in Goose Creek, outside Charleston. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7439792368939665259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
